        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681050971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17109793396790884501">Well, here it is: the conclusion to the wonderful, tragically underrated New Sun series by Mr. Wolfe. This book came out a few years after the previous one, and serves as a sort of capper to the whole thing- kind of anyways. It also works, a bit, as a stand alone tale. You don't have to read the other four to enjoy this one, but it helps, because the book is batshit insane at parts, and is one of the most dense bits of literature I have ever read.<br/><br/>It takes the wacky, obscure, completely otherworl</span>
  <span id="freeText17109793396790884501" style="display:none">Well, here it is: the conclusion to the wonderful, tragically underrated New Sun series by Mr. Wolfe. This book came out a few years after the previous one, and serves as a sort of capper to the whole thing- kind of anyways. It also works, a bit, as a stand alone tale. You don't have to read the other four to enjoy this one, but it helps, because the book is batshit insane at parts, and is one of the most dense bits of literature I have ever read.<br /><br />It takes the wacky, obscure, completely otherworldy vibe of the last four books and takes it up about a million notches by adding in a time travelling element. Because, you know, the series was just making too much sense beforehand ;)<br /><br />If you loved, or even just liked, the first four books, pick this up and see what happens to Severian. I really enjoyed how the author took some serious risks in this book. For example, it starts off at least 10 years after the last one (but could be much longer because time keeps changing here), and the story mentions off handed things that have happened over that time, but in ways that assume that you, the reader, will know about them. But of course you don't, because they happened between the fourth and fifth book. Severian, the narrator, also has a hard time remembering that, so it takes the idea of an unreliable narrator to a whole other level. Worth checking out for that trick alone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17109793396790884501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_168584052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168584052" />
    <a title="Max" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1705583-max"><img alt="Max" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476974241p2/1705583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168584052?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Max" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Max" href="/user/show/1705583-max">Max</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780312930332" href="/book/show/3215235-the-urth-of-the-new-sun">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1705583-max?shelf=sf">sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168584052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2119890086554423215">I feel inclined to give this book a lower rating because I found it to be so much weaker than the rest of the New Sun series (and however much people describe it as a 'coda' or 'not really a sequel,' it really is a direct sequel), but I don't really think that would be fair—it's still much better than a lot of the science fiction out there. That's the thing, though: where the other books in the New Sun cycle weren't so heavy on the S part of SF, this book is more heavily sciencey science fiction</span>
  <span id="freeText2119890086554423215" style="display:none">I feel inclined to give this book a lower rating because I found it to be so much weaker than the rest of the New Sun series (and however much people describe it as a 'coda' or 'not really a sequel,' it really is a direct sequel), but I don't really think that would be fair—it's still much better than a lot of the science fiction out there. That's the thing, though: where the other books in the New Sun cycle weren't so heavy on the S part of SF, this book is more heavily sciencey science fiction. That's not a criticism in and of itself, but I feel like Wolfe's writing is just better when the plot is a bit more down to Ea(U)rth. Indeed, the latter section of the book that's set on Urth was much more enjoyable to me, in spite of the ridiculous heavy-handedness with which Severian's life is paralleled to Jesus's. I think really what felt off to me about this book was that it consisted of barely anything but clarifications and answers, and what I liked about the other New Sun books was their dense, barely penetrable air of mystery and confusion. To have things tied up so neatly was...a bit disappointing. Still, it's Wolfe, so there's first-class writing all around.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2119890086554423215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1173372099" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4477868402425481346">This has to be one of the most original and complex stories I’ve ever heard (read). I have no clue how anyone could walk away reading just the first four books. Urth of the New Sun did shine light on many, many questions that remained after the fourth book though I still had to read the synopsis and look up a few things in the Lexicon Urthus when I was done with Urth of the New Sun to truly get closure. The inspiration from Wolfe’s faith goes all out in this book compared to the first four, but </span>
  <span id="freeText4477868402425481346" style="display:none">This has to be one of the most original and complex stories I’ve ever heard (read). I have no clue how anyone could walk away reading just the first four books. Urth of the New Sun did shine light on many, many questions that remained after the fourth book though I still had to read the synopsis and look up a few things in the Lexicon Urthus when I was done with Urth of the New Sun to truly get closure. The inspiration from Wolfe’s faith goes all out in this book compared to the first four, but I don’t really mind it that much. It’s one of the most interesting and complex universes I’ve ever set my imaginary foot in.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1765458346" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1765458346" />
    <a title="Yve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3730637-yve"><img alt="Yve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584449652p2/3730637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1765458346?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yve" href="/user/show/3730637-yve">Yve</a>

  <span id="freeText5346001042677174945" style="display:none">Using this space for some second-time-around notes.<br /><br />1. It's appropriate that the epigraph is taken from a translation that is known to be a distortion of the original, and credited to the translator alone (FitzGerald's Rubaiyat of Omar Khayyam).<br /><br />2. And a verse from the same poem:<br /><blockquote>I sometimes think that never blows so red<br />The Rose as where some buried Caesar bled;<br />That every Hyacinth the garden wears<br />Dropt in its Lap from some once lovely Head.</blockquote><br /><br />3. Gunnie swears by the Danaides, one of whom was named Scylla, and one of whose victims was named Idas. <br /><br />4. Sidero means "iron" from the Greek root but "stars" from the Latin root.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=literature">literature</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer580206887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1592647799406016129">A companion piece to The Book of the New Sun, set in a giant generation-spanning spaceship, this book is equally mysterious and fascinating. Not quite as easy to understand and absorb, but certainly a worthy read. Not sure how well it works as a stand-alone novel, though.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Gl/YM5ORT0OAjvE2FOZzJteIxsiVMt7B5ycCPgKDgGQQmaNsMtS5j9Uqh3jRAaOLPuzADWbNOcxUq0xlu8yeaQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x3m11vnSBtZf3Nno1T7brN3KcdQjtdLDPXH+1GVS/JPNv86JWJfwGgp4r6YQ2QsBNK53EdBKNc6O/bCP3B3ing==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/23069.Gene_Wolfe">About Gene Wolfe</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/23069.Gene_Wolfe"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1556979018p3/23069.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/23069.Gene_Wolfe">Gene Wolfe
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,402
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10291632356280433104">Gene Wolfe was an American science fiction and fantasy writer. He was noted for his dense, allusive prose as well as the strong influence of his Catholic faith, to which he converted after marrying a Catholic. He was a prolific short story writer and a novelist, and has won many awards in the field.<br/><br/>The Damon Knight Memorial Grand Master Award is given by SFWA for ‘lifetime achievement in science f</span>
  <span id="freeText10291632356280433104" style="display:none">Gene Wolfe was an American science fiction and fantasy writer. He was noted for his dense, allusive prose as well as the strong influence of his Catholic faith, to which he converted after marrying a Catholic. He was a prolific short story writer and a novelist, and has won many awards in the field.<br /><br />The Damon Knight Memorial Grand Master Award is given by SFWA for ‘lifetime achievement in science fiction and/or fantasy.’ Wolfe joins the Grand Master ranks alongside such legends as Connie Willis, Michael Moorcock, Anne McCaffrey, Robert Silverberg, Ursula K. Le Guin, Isaac Asimov, Ray Bradbury and Joe Haldeman. The award will be presented at the 48th Annual Nebula Awards Weekend in San Jose, CA, May 16-19, 2013.<br /><br />While attending Texas A&amp;M University Wolfe published his first speculative fiction in The Commentator, a student literary journal. Wolfe dropped out during his junior year, and was drafted to fight in the Korean War. After returning to the United States he earned a degree from the University of Houston and became an industrial engineer. He edited the journal Plant Engineering for many years before retiring to write full-time, but his most famous professional engineering achievement is a contribution to the machine used to make Pringles potato crisps. He lived in Barrington, Illinois, a suburb of Chicago.<br /><br />A frequent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/award/show/9-hugo-award" rel="nofollow noopener">Hugo</a> nominee without a win, Wolfe has nevertheless picked up several <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/award/show/23-nebula-award" rel="nofollow noopener">Nebula</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/award/show/46-locus-award" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus</a> Awards, among others, including the World Fantasy Award for Life Achievement and the 2012 Damon Knight Memorial Grand Master Award. He is also a member of the Science Fiction Hall of Fame.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/genewolfe">http://us.macmillan.com/author/genewolfe</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10291632356280433104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
